## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population size through density-dependent feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Exponential (Malthusian) growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited growth where rate is proportional to current population'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreases logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Growth with minimum viable population threshold (strong Allee effect)'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Generalized asymmetric sigmoidal growth model'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth as balance between anabolism and catabolism with different scaling'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Growth rate scales as a power of population size'}
- {'name': 'Logistic with time-dependent rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with exponentially changing intrinsic rate'}
- {'name': 'Harvesting/immigration offset', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with constant immigration or harvesting'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2', 'scenario': 'Growth with linear and quadratic population-dependent terms'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth with saturating reproduction and linear mortality'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent negative feedback → Polynomial terms like P*(1 - c*P) or P*log(c/P) causing growth to slow at high P
- Allee effects (positive density dependence at low P) → Cubic terms P*(P-c1)*(c2-P) creating growth suppression at both low and high P
- Metabolic scaling in growth → Fractional power laws P**c with c between 0.5 and 1 reflecting allometric scaling
- Carrying capacity structure → Growth rate equals zero at specific P values, indicated by factored polynomial in P
- Time-varying environment → Multiplicative modulation by periodic sin(c*t) or trend exp(c*t) terms on top of density-dependent structure
- Balance of gain and loss processes → Difference of two power laws c0*P**a - c1*P**b representing competing biological processes
- Weak vs strong density dependence → Exponent on (1 - P/K)**theta: theta<1 gives early saturation, theta>1 delays saturation
- Immigration/emigration signatures → Additive constants or terms independent of P in the growth rate equation

Matched candidates: ["P*(c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1))"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

**GT expression:**
```
0.8678*(-1 + P/6.058)*(1 - P/14.185)*P + 0.8678*P^(1/3) + 0.8678*P
```

Let me expand the cubic part:
(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185) = -1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P²/(6.058×14.185)

So the first term = 0.8678*P*[-1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P²/(6.058×14.185)]
= 0.8678*[-P + P²/14.185 + P²/6.058 - P³/(85.92)]

This gives us: **GT = aP³ + bP² + cP + dP^(1/3)** where a,b,c,d are specific constants.

More precisely:
- P³ coefficient: -0.8678/(6.058×14.185) ≈ -0.01010
- P² coefficient: 0.8678*(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) ≈ 0.8678*0.2353 ≈ 0.2042
- P coefficient: 0.8678*(-1) + 0.8678 = 0
- P^(1/3) coefficient: 0.8678

So **GT = aP³ + bP² + dP^(1/3)** (the linear P terms cancel!)

Wait, let me recheck. The GT has three parts:
1. 0.8678*(-1 + P/6.058)*(1 - P/14.185)*P
2. 0.8678*P^(1/3)
3. 0.8678*P

The linear term from part 1: 0.8678*P*(-1) = -0.8678*P
Part 3: +0.8678*P
These cancel! So GT = aP³ + bP² + 0.8678*P^(1/3)

So **GT = αP³ + βP² + γP^(1/3)** where α < 0, β > 0, γ > 0.

The key basis functions are: **P³, P², P^(1/3)**.

Now I need to check which candidates can produce exactly this combination.

Let me systematically go through candidates, focusing on those that could potentially have P^(1/3):

Candidates with P**c (power law terms): 45, 46, 47, 48, 71, 72, 73, 77, 78, 79, 89, 90, etc.

**Candidate 78: P*(P*c0 + c1) + P**c2*c3**
= c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^c2

Set c2 = 1/3, then we get c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^(1/3). But GT has no linear P term (it cancelled) and has a P³ term. This has P² and P but no P³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 77: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P**c2*c3**
Same as 78 essentially. No P³ term. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 48: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P**c2*c3 + c4**
= c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^c2 + c4. No P³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 47: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2 + P**c3*c4 + c5**
= c0*P² + (c1+c2)*P + c4*P^c3 + c5. No P³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 73: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + P*c3 + P**c4*c5**
= c0*P*(P*c1)^c2 - c0*P + c3*P + c5*P^c4
= c0*c1^c2 * P^(1+c2) + (c3-c0)*P + c5*P^c4

Set c2=2 → c0*c1²*P³, and c4=1/3 → c5*P^(1/3), and c3=c0 to kill linear term.
This gives: αP³ + 0*P + γP^(1/3). But GT also has βP². Missing P². **NO MATCH** unless... wait, we need P² too.

**Candidate 89: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + P**c3*c4**
= c0*c1^c2 * P^(1+c2) - c0*P + c4*P^c3
Only two power-law terms plus P. Can't get three independent terms (P³, P², P^(1/3)). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 52: P*(c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1))**
= P*[c0*(P*c1)^c2 - c0 + c3*(P² + ...)]
= c0*c1^c2*P^(1+c2) + c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + ... 

Set c2 = -2/3: P^(1/3) term. Then we have P^(1/3) + cubic + quadratic + linear + constant*P terms. This could work!

P*(c0*((P*c1)^c2 - 1) + c3*(P+c4)*(P*c5+1))
= P*(c0*(P*c1)^c2 - c0 + c3*(P²*c5 + P + c4*P*c5 + c4))
= c0*c1^c2 * P^(1+c2) - c0*P + c3*c5*P³ + c3*P² + c3*c4*c5*P² + c3*c4*P
= c0*c1^c2 * P^(1+c2) + c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + (-c0+c3*c4)*P

Set c2 = -2/3: get P^(1/3) ✓
P³ term: c3*c5 = α ✓
P² term: c3*(1+c4*c5) = β ✓
P term: -c0+c3*c4 = 0 → c0 = c3*c4 ✓

This has enough free constants! **MATCH.**

**Candidate 51: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + P*c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1) - 1**
= c0*c1^c2*P^(1+c2) - c0*P + c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + c3*c4*P - 1

Same as 52 but with a constant -1. GT has no constant term. **NO MATCH.**

Let me now check candidates with rational forms that could simplify to P³ + P² + P^(1/3).

Actually, P^(1/3) cannot come from rational functions, exponentials, logs, or sin. So I need candidates that explicitly have a power-law P**c term or equivalent.

Let me list candidates with P**c or similar:
- 45, 46, 47, 48, 64, 70, 71, 72, 73, 74, 75, 77, 78, 79, 80, 89, 90, 92

**Candidate 46: P*(P*c0 + c1) + P**c2*c3 + c4*exp(P**2*c5)**
= c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^c2 + c4*exp(c5*P²)
Has exp term that can't be zeroed without losing everything. Set c4=0: c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^c2. Missing P³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 45: P*c0 + P*(P*c1 + c2) + P**c3*c4 + c5*exp(P**2*c6)**
= c1*P² + (c0+c2)*P + c4*P^c3 + c5*exp(c6*P²). Set c5=0: same issue, no P³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 79: P*c0 + P*(P*c1 + c2) + P**c3*c4**
= c1*P² + (c0+c2)*P + c4*P^c3. No P³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 71: (P*c0*(P + c1) + P*(P*c2 + c3) + P**c4*c5*(P + c1))/(P + c1)**
= P*c0 + P*(P*c2+c3)/(P+c1) + c5*P^c4

Expanding P*(P*c2+c3)/(P+c1): do polynomial division.
P*(P*c2+c3)/(P+c1) = c2*P + (c3-c1*c2)*P/(P+c1) = c2*P + (c3-c1*c2)*(1 - c1/(P+c1))*... 

Actually this doesn't simplify to a polynomial. So this has a rational part. **NO MATCH** (rational functions can't produce P^(1/3) behavior and polynomial simultaneously in exact form).

Wait, let me reconsider. The full expression:
= [P*c0*(P+c1) + P*(P*c2+c3) + c5*P^c4*(P+c1)] / (P+c1)
= P*c0 + [P*(P*c2+c3)]/(P+c1) + c5*P^c4

The middle term is not polynomial. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 72: (P*(P*c0 + c1) + P**c2*c3*(P + c4))/(P + c4)**
= [c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^c2*(P+c4)] / (P+c4)
= [c0*P² + c1*P]/(P+c4) + c3*P^c2

The rational part [c0*P² + c1*P]/(P+c4) = c0*P + (c1-c0*c4)*P/(P+c4) = c0*P + (c1-c0*c4)*(1 - c4/(P+c4))

This doesn't simplify to a polynomial. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 90: P*(P*c0 + c1) + P**c2*c3*log(P*c4 + 1) + c5*exp(P**2*c6)**
Has log and exp. Set c5=0: P²*c0 + P*c1 + c3*P^c2*log(c4*P+1). The log*power term can't equal P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 70: P*(P**2*c0*exp(P*c1) + c2*((P*c3)**c4 - 1))**
= c0*P³*exp(c1*P) + c2*c3^c4*P^(1+c4) - c2*P

Set c1=0: c0*P³ + c2*c3^c4*P^(1+c4) - c2*P
Set c4 = -2/3: P^(1/3) term. Then: c0*P³ + A*P^(1/3) - c2*P
Missing P². **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 80: P*(c0*(P + c1)*((P*c2)**c3 - 1) + c4)/(P + c1)**
= P*[c0*((P*c2)^c3 - 1) + c4/(P+c1)]... wait:
= P*[c0*(P+c1)*((P*c2)^c3 - 1) + c4] / (P+c1)
= P*c0*((P*c2)^c3 - 1) + P*c4/(P+c1)

The second term is rational, not polynomial. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 92: (P*c0 + (P*c1 + 1)*(P*c2*(sqrt(P*c3) - 1) - 1))/(P*c1 + 1)**
= P*c0/(P*c1+1) + P*c2*(sqrt(c3*P) - 1) - 1
Has sqrt(P) = P^(1/2), not P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 64: P*c0*(P*c1 - 1) + P**c2*c3*log(P*c4 + 1) - 1**
= c0*c1*P² - c0*P + c3*P^c2*log(c4*P+1) - 1. The log term can't produce P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 74: P*c0*(P*c1 + 1)*exp(c2*t) + P*c3 + P**c4*c5**
Has t dependence. Set c0=0 (or c2→-∞... no). If c0=0: P*c3 + c5*P^c4. Only two terms. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 75: P*(c0*(P*c1 + 1)*exp(c2*t) + c3*((P*c4)**c5 - 1))**
Set c0=0: P*c3*((P*c4)^c5 - 1) = c3*c4^c5*P^(1+c5) - c3*P. Two terms. **NO MATCH.**

Now let me reconsider **Candidate 52** more carefully:

GT = αP³ + βP² + γP^(1/3) where:
- α = -0.8678/(6.058×14.185) ≈ -0.01010
- β = 0.8678*(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) ≈ 0.2042  
- γ = 0.8678

Candidate 52: P*(c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1))

Expanding:
= P*[c0*(P*c1)^c2 - c0 + c3*(P²*c5 + P + c4*c5*P + c4)]
= c0*c1^c2 * P^(1+c2) + c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + (c3*c4 - c0)*P

Set c2 = -2/3: P^(1+c2) = P^(1/3) ✓
Set c3*c4 = c0 to kill linear term ✓
c3*c5 = α ✓
c3*(1+c4*c5) = β ✓
c0*c1^(-2/3) = γ ✓

We have 6 constants (c0-c5) and 5 equations (including c2=-2/3). This is solvable. **MATCH!**

Now let me check **Candidate 95: P*c0*(P + c1)*(P*c2 + 1)**
= c0*c2*P³ + c0*(1+c1*c2)*P² + c0*c1*P
This is a cubic polynomial in P. No P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 93, 94**: Pure polynomials. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 53: P*(P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3)/(P + c4)**
This is a rational function. Can't produce P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 100: (P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3)/(P + c4)**
Rational function. **NO MATCH.**

Let me check all remaining candidates with P**c type terms that I haven't checked:

**Candidate 97: P*c0*(sqrt(P*c1) - 1) + c2*log(P*c3 + 1) - 1**
= c0*sqrt(c1)*P^(3/2) - c0*P + c2*log(c3*P+1) - 1. Has P^(3/2) and log, not P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

Now let me verify candidates without P^(1/3) can't match. The GT has P^(1/3) which is a fractional power. No combination of polynomials, exponentials, logs, sin, rational functions can produce P^(1/3) exactly. So I only need to check candidates that have a free power P**c.

Going through systematically, candidates with P**c or (P*c)**c:
45, 46, 47, 48, 51, 52, 58, 59, 64, 70, 71, 72, 73, 74, 75, 77, 78, 79, 80, 89, 90, 92, 97

I've checked most. Let me check the remaining:

**Candidate 58: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*log(P*c4 + 1)**
= c0*c1^c2*P^(1+c2) - c0*P + c3*log(c4*P+1)
Set c2=-2/3: A*P^(1/3) - c0*P + c3*log(c4*P+1). Log can't produce P² and P³. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 59: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*sin(P*c4 + c5)**
Similar issue. Sin can't produce polynomial terms. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 88: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*exp(P*c4) - 1**
Exp can't produce polynomial terms exactly. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 73: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + P*c3 + P**c4*c5**
= c0*c1^c2*P^(1+c2) - c0*P + c3*P + c5*P^c4
= c0*c1^c2*P^(1+c2) + (c3-c0)*P + c5*P^c4

Two power terms plus linear. Set c2=-2/3 → P^(1/3), c4=3 → P³. Then: A*P^(1/3) + B*P + C*P³. Missing P². 

Or set c2=1 → P², c4=1/3 → P^(1/3). Then: A*P² + B*P + C*P^(1/3). Missing P³.

Can't get all four needed terms (P³, P², P^(1/3), and zero P). **NO MATCH.**

Actually wait - if we set c2=1 → P^2, c4=1/3 → P^(1/3): A*P² + (c3-c0)*P + c5*P^(1/3). We need (c3-c0)=0 and no P³. But GT has P³ term. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 89: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + P**c3*c4**
= c0*c1^c2*P^(1+c2) - c0*P + c4*P^c3
Two power terms + linear. Same issue as 73. **NO MATCH.**

Now let me check **Candidate 5: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*sin(c4*log(P*c5 + 1) + c6) - 1**
Has sin(log(...)) which can't produce polynomial terms. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 9: P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*exp(P**c4*c5) - 1**
Exp can't produce polynomial terms. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 19: (P*c0*(P*c1)^c2 - 1)*(P*c3 + c4) + P*c5 + c6) / (P*c3 + c4)**
Wait, let me re-read: (P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1)*(P*c3 + c4) + P*c5 + c6)/(P*c3 + c4)
= P*c0*((P*c1)^c2 - 1) + (P*c5 + c6)/(P*c3 + c4)

The rational part (P*c5+c6)/(P*c3+c4) = c5/c3 + (c6-c4*c5/c3)/(P*c3+c4). This is not polynomial. **NO MATCH.**

Now let me look at candidates that might produce P^(1/3) through other means. Actually, none of the remaining candidates have free power exponents except those I've already checked.

Let me verify **Candidate 52** is the only match by double-checking my expansion:

Candidate 52: P*(c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1))

Let me set c2 = -2/3.

Inner expression: c0*((P*c1)^(-2/3) - 1) + c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1)
= c0*c1^(-2/3)*P^(-2/3) - c0 + c3*(P²*c5 + P + c4*c5*P + c4)
= c0*c1^(-2/3)*P^(-2/3) - c0 + c3*c5*P² + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P + c3*c4

Multiply by P:
= c0*c1^(-2/3)*P^(1/3) - c0*P + c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + c3*c4*P
= c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + (c3*c4 - c0)*P + c0*c1^(-2/3)*P^(1/3)

GT = αP³ + βP² + 0*P + γP^(1/3)

Equations:
1. c3*c5 = α
2. c3*(1+c4*c5) = β
3. c3*c4 - c0 = 0 → c0 = c3*c4
4. c0*c1^(-2/3) = γ

From (3): c0 = c3*c4
From (1): c5 = α/c3
From (2): c3 + c3*c4*c5 = β → c3 + c0*α/c3 = β → c3 + c4*α = β
From (4): c3*c4*c1^(-2/3) = γ

Choose c3 freely (say c3 = 1):
- c5 = α
- c4 = (β - 1)/1... wait, c3 + c4*α = β → 1 + c4*α = β → c4 = (β-1)/α
- c0 = c4 = (β-1)/α
- c1^(-2/3) = γ/c0 → c1 = (c0/γ)^(3/2)

All real-valued. ✓ **MATCH confirmed.**

Now let me also check **Candidate 51** again:
P*c0*((P*c1)**c2 - 1) + P*c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1) - 1

= c0*c1^c2*P^(1+c2) - c0*P + c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + c3*c4*P - 1

This has a constant term -1. GT has no constant term. The -1 is hardcoded, not a free constant. **NO MATCH.**

Let me also check **Candidate 65: P*(c0*(P*c1 + 1)*exp(c2*t) + c3*(P + c4)*(P*c5 + 1))**
Set c0=0: P*c3*(P+c4)*(P*c5+1) = c3*c5*P³ + c3*(1+c4*c5)*P² + c3*c4*P. Cubic polynomial, no P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 86: P*(c0*(P + c1)*(P*c2 + 1) + t*(P*c3 + c4))**
Has t. Set coefficient of t to 0 needs c3=c4=0 (since it's t*(P*c3+c4)). Then: P*c0*(P+c1)*(P*c2+1) = cubic polynomial. No P^(1/3). **NO MATCH.**

Let me now quickly verify all remaining candidates don't have P^(1/3) capability:

Candidates 1-4, 6-8, 10-18, 20-44, 49-50, 53-57, 60-63, 65-69, 76, 81-88, 91, 93-96, 98-104:

None of these have a free power exponent P**c where c is a free constant. They use polynomials, exp, log, sin, rational functions, or sqrt (which gives P^(1/2), not P^(1/3)).

The only exception might be candidates using log(exp(...)+1) which is softplus - still can't produce P^(1/3).

So the only match is **Candidate 52**.
